# I. SHOCK-EVENT SIMULATIONS

*(What actually happens when the system is hit)*

Each simulation is written as a **state machine**, not a story.

---

## 1. BANK FAILURE / CAPITAL FREEZE

### TRIGGER CONDITIONS

* Primary bank insolvency
* Account access frozen > 24 hours
* Payment rails unavailable
* Counterparty failure

---

### STATE MACHINE

```
NORMAL
  ‚Üì (Bank access lost)
CAPITAL SHOCK
  ‚Üì
CONTAINMENT
  ‚Üì
REDUNDANCY ACTIVATION
  ‚Üì
STABILIZATION
  ‚Üì
RETURN / REBALANCE
```

---

### ACTION SEQUENCE

**T+0‚Äì24 HOURS (CONTAINMENT)**

* Freeze all non-essential spend
* Activate secondary banking accounts
* Lock capital ledger (read-only)
* OVCS assumes capital authority

**T+24‚Äì72 HOURS (REDUNDANCY)**

* Route revenue to backup accounts
* Draw on survival reserve
* Delay payroll if legally permitted
* Notify board (facts only)

**T+3‚Äì14 DAYS (STABILIZATION)**

* Replace banking partner
* Reallocate capital pools
* Adjust runway models
* Archive incident report

---

### SYSTEM OUTCOME

* No new programs launched
* No equity or comp changes
* Survival preserved
* Trust maintained

---

## 2. FOUNDER LOSS (INCAPACITY OR DEATH)

*(Summarized here; detailed protocol already defined)*

### STATE MACHINE

```
NORMAL
  ‚Üì (Founder unavailable)
AUTHORITY SUSPENSION
  ‚Üì
INTERIM STEWARDSHIP
  ‚Üì
CONTINUITY DECISION
  ‚Üì
SUCCESSION / WIND-DOWN
```

---

### ACTION SEQUENCE (FIRST 72 HOURS)

* OVCS assumes supreme authority
* Archive frozen
* Banking & signing authority locked
* Interim Steward appointed
* Internal notice issued

---

### DECISION POINT (‚â§ 90 DAYS)

* Continue as-is
* Collective stewardship
* Orderly wind-down

Founder equity **does not accelerate**.
Heirs receive **economic interest only**.

---

## 3. REGULATORY / LEGAL ATTACK

### TRIGGERS

* Subpoena
* Regulatory inquiry
* License suspension
* Political/legal harassment

---

### STATE MACHINE

```
NORMAL
  ‚Üì
LEGAL SHOCK
  ‚Üì
DEFENSIVE MODE
  ‚Üì
COMPLIANCE / CONTEST
  ‚Üì
RESOLUTION
```

---

### ACTION SEQUENCE

**IMMEDIATE**

* Halt affected operations
* Retain counsel
* Preserve all records
* Public silence

**MID-TERM**

* Separate affected entity
* Firewall other coops
* Shift programs if needed

**RESOLUTION**

* Comply, contest, or exit jurisdiction
* Update doctrine
* Archive precedent

---

### SYSTEM RULE

> **The federation survives even if one node is sacrificed.**

---

# II. ARCHIVE OS ‚Äî CANONICAL SCHEMA

*(Objects, states, transitions)*

This is the **memory engine** of the ecosystem.

---

## CORE OBJECT TYPES

```
OBJECTS
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Decision
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Policy
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Strategy
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Program
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Asset
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Capital Allocation
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Risk
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Incident
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Role
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Authority
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Entity
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Person
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Knowledge Artifact
```

---

## UNIVERSAL OBJECT STATES

Every object follows the same lifecycle:

```
DRAFT
  ‚Üì
REVIEW
  ‚Üì
ACTIVE
  ‚Üì
SUPERSEDED or SUNSET
  ‚Üì
ARCHIVED (immutable)
```

---

## KEY OBJECT DEFINITIONS

### DECISION

* Fields: owner, authority, rationale, impact, date
* Rule: **No decision without authority reference**

### ASSET

* Fields: type, owner, steward, value, maintenance cost
* Rule: **Unmaintained assets must sunset**

### CAPITAL ALLOCATION

* Fields: source, restrictions, tranche, owner, expiry
* Rule: **Every allocation has a kill-switch**

### INCIDENT

* Fields: trigger, scope, response, outcome
* Rule: **Incidents create doctrine**

---

## TRANSITIONS (EXAMPLES)

```
Decision: DRAFT ‚Üí ACTIVE
  Requires: Authority + Archive entry

Asset: ACTIVE ‚Üí SUNSET
  Trigger: Cost > Value or Mission Drift

Program: ACTIVE ‚Üí ARCHIVED
  Trigger: Time-bound completion or failure
```

---

## ARCHIVE AXIOM

> **If it is not in the Archive, it did not happen.
> If it cannot be archived, it must not happen.**

# REGULATORY & LEGAL ATTACK DOCTRINE

*(Mitigation, containment, survival, adaptation)*

---

## I. THREAT MODEL (WHAT WE ASSUME IS POSSIBLE)

We assume **good faith regulation** *and* **bad faith attack** are indistinguishable at the outset.

### Attack Vectors

* Licensing / registration challenges
* Banking and financial controls
* Employment classification audits
* Securities / capital-raising inquiries
* Zoning / land-use / environmental enforcement
* Tax authority audits
* Political or reputational lawfare
* Injunctions to halt operations

**System assumption:**

> Any node can be attacked; the federation must survive loss of nodes.

---

## II. CORE DEFENSE PRINCIPLES (NON-NEGOTIABLE)

1. **Containment before defense**
2. **Federation over monolith**
3. **Separation of capital, authority, and labor**
4. **Jurisdictional optionality**
5. **Documentation as armor**
6. **Sacrificial subsidiaries are acceptable**

---

## III. PRE-ATTACK MITIGATION (BUILT-IN IMMUNITY)

### 1. STRUCTURAL MITIGATION (DESIGN-TIME)

```
[Regulators] ‚îÄ‚îÄX‚îÄ‚îÄ> [Single Coop]
                     ‚Üì
             [Federated Coops]
                     ‚Üì
           [Autonomous Legal Nodes]
```

**Mitigation Techniques**

* Each coop is:

  * Separately incorporated
  * Separately banked
  * Separately licensed where required
* No shared payroll across regulated lines
* No universal operating license
* Capital participants are non-members (Class F)

**Outcome:**

> An attack on one entity does not propagate.

---

### 2. CAPITAL & FINANCIAL MITIGATION

* Multiple banks (credit union + commercial)
* Multiple payment rails
* Survival reserves outside operating accounts
* Restricted trusts legally insulated
* No commingling between:

  * Investment capital
  * Program funds
  * Operating payroll

**Outcome:**

> Regulators can freeze an account, not the system.

---

### 3. ROLE & EMPLOYMENT MITIGATION

* Clear worker vs steward vs board vs founder roles
* Contractors where appropriate
* Apprentices clearly non-employees
* Written authority boundaries
* No ‚Äúshadow management‚Äù

**Outcome:**

> Employment audits fail to pierce structure.

---

### 4. DOCUMENTATION MITIGATION (ARCHIVE OS)

Every regulated activity has:

* A policy
* An authority
* A record
* A version history

**Outcome:**

> Discovery favors us.

---

## IV. ACTIVE ATTACK RESPONSE (WHEN IT HITS)

---

## A. UNIVERSAL FIRST 48 HOURS (ALL ATTACK TYPES)

```
TRIGGER
  ‚Üì
LEGAL FREEZE
  ‚Üì
AUTHORITY CONSOLIDATION
  ‚Üì
COMMUNICATION SILENCE
```

### Actions

* Halt affected operations immediately
* Freeze Archive objects (read-only)
* OVCS assumes authority
* Retain counsel (jurisdiction-specific)
* No public statements
* No internal speculation

---

## B. ATTACK-SPECIFIC PLAYBOOKS

---

### 1. FINANCIAL REGULATORY ATTACK (BANKING, SEC, AML)

**Examples**

* Account freezes
* Capital questioning
* Investment structure scrutiny

**Mitigation**

* Shift cash flow to unaffected entities
* Activate credit union rails
* Suspend capital intake
* Demonstrate segregation
* If needed: spin off or liquidate targeted vehicle

**Doctrine Rule**

> Capital pauses; operations continue.

---

### 2. EMPLOYMENT / LABOR ATTACK

**Examples**

* Worker misclassification claims
* Wage/hour audits

**Mitigation**

* Produce role charters
* Produce task logs
* Demonstrate member-owner distinctions
* Reassign functions temporarily
* Exit jurisdictions if necessary

**Doctrine Rule**

> Labor adapts faster than law.

---

### 3. LICENSING / ZONING / ENVIRONMENTAL ATTACK

**Examples**

* Makerspaces, factories, land use

**Mitigation**

* Pause physical operations
* Shift to research / design
* Lease or relocate
* Spin down affected site
* Preserve IP centrally

**Doctrine Rule**

> Physical nodes are expendable; knowledge is not.

---

### 4. TAX AUTHORITY ATTACK

**Examples**

* Audits, penalties, reclassification

**Mitigation**

* Produce ledgers and doctrine
* Demonstrate nonprofit vs coop separation
* Negotiate, settle, or restructure
* Close and reincorporate if required

**Doctrine Rule**

> Entities are renewable.

---

## V. FEDERATION FIREWALLING (CRITICAL)

```
[Attacked Entity]
      |
      X  (Legal Firewall)
      |
[Other Coops Continue]
```

**Mechanisms**

* No cross-guarantees
* No shared debt
* No shared licenses
* No shared officers where risky

**Outcome:**

> The blast radius is bounded.

# üåç 1) OVERALL CAPITAL ECOSYSTEM ARCHITECTURE

```
   ‚Üì

   ‚Üì

   ‚Üì
CAPITAL FEEDBACK / RETURNS / GROWTH

```

Each zone has **actors (who)**, **activities (what)**, and **mechanisms (how)**.

# ‚öôÔ∏è 3) WHAT ‚Äî Capital Types & Units

Your ecosystem handles **multiple capital forms**:

**1. Deferred Compensation Units (DCUs)**
‚Ä¢ Work credits representing produced human/labor value
‚Ä¢ *Transitional internal capital* ‚Äî convertible to equity, incentives

**2. Equity Units**
‚Ä¢ Ownership interests in ventures / coops
‚Ä¢ Represent *future claim to surplus / dividends*

**3. Capital Units**
‚Ä¢ Cooperative capital pool shares
‚Ä¢ Voting & surplus participations

**4. Fund & LP Interests**
‚Ä¢ Shares in funds, SPVs, portfolio vehicles

**5. Asset Holdings**
‚Ä¢ Cash, bonds, stocks, real estate, IP rights

**6. IP Credits / Commons Credits**
‚Ä¢ Value stored in shared intellectual resources

**7. Revenue Share Rights**
‚Ä¢ Future operational income claims

These are **all tracked by UCUC** (central ledger), and are subject to governance tagging, tranche conditions, and risk constraints.

---

# üîÑ 4) HOW ‚Äî Lifecycle of Capital Across the Ecosystem

### üå± **A) Generation & Production (Creation of Capital)**

Capital is *generated* from:

1. **Work Output (DCU Creation)**

   * Worker-Members (Class A) produce value via tasks/roles.
   * DCUs are awarded and tracked, pending conversion.

2. **Studio Value Production**

   * Idea ‚Üí Prototype ‚Üí MVP via OVCS+studios (IDEA Labs, Hackerspace, Maker/Fablab)
   * Converts studio output into asset value (software, IP, product roadmap milestones).

3. **Funding Inputs**

   * Capital Participants (Class F) contribute cash/equity.
   * External investors allocate into Mande / funds.

4. **Asset Appreciation**

   * Real estate, stocks, bonds increase in value.
   * Returns feed back as capital gains.

5. **Commons Ecosystem Contributions**

   * Shared tooling, rights, standards improve efficiency.
   * IP credits and commons credits store long-term value.

> **Result:** Capital units across multiple types are produced and *stored* in the ecosystem‚Äôs ledger.

---

### üß† **B) Allocation (Decision on Where Capital Goes)**

Capital allocation decisions are *governed*, *hierarchical*, *conditional*, and *strategic*.

**Key Allocation Actors**

* **Entity Councils** ‚Äî evaluate local needs.
* **Boards (Class C)** ‚Äî approve major allocations.
* **OVCS Authority** ‚Äî certifies that allocation aligns with doctrine/policy.
* **Mande Investment Group** ‚Äî proposes strategic deployments.
* **UCUC** ‚Äî executes allocation on ledger.

**Allocation Pathways**

1. **Survival Capital**
   Ensures:

   * Legal/insurance compliance
   * Security & infra
   * Runway buffer

2. **Coherence Capital**
   Builds:

   * Governance OS
   * Standards & templates
   * Training & documentation

3. **Execution Capital**
   Funds:

   * Staff hiring
   * Program pilots (Msingi cycle: Kano, Ndebe, Kuzu, Zalendo, Zamba, Luma)
   * Core product builds

4. **Expansion Capital**
   Enables:

   * New studios
   * New markets/ventures
   * Experimental lines

**Rules**

* Always priority: survival ‚Üí coherence ‚Üí execution ‚Üí expansion
* Approval linked to success criteria & exit conditions
* Funds released in *tranches with milestones*
* Niguvu monitors for policy violations

---

### ‚ö° **C) Use / Consumption of Capital**

Capital is consumed by:

**1. Labor & Operations**

* Salaries
* Tools, platforms, infra

**2. Programs**

* Msingi cycle programs operational budgets

**3. Product Development**

* Studio outputs
* Tech and physical infrastructure

**4. Growth Activities**

* Marketing/community
* Strategic partnerships

**5. Asset Purchases**

* Reinvestment in IP, real estate, portfolios

**6. Operational Expenses**

* Insurance, compliance, security

Consumption is tracked and compared to allocated tranches; variance requires governance re-approval.

---

### üìà **D) Feedback & Value Realization**

As capital is used, value streams back into the ecosystem:

**1) Revenue Generation**

* Clients/customers pay for products & services.
* Revenue flows into venture accounts.

**2) Capital Growth**

* Investment returns (Mande portfolios)
* Asset appreciation

**3) Reinvestment**

* Surpluses reallocated to high-value activities

**4) Capital Restoration**

* Returns replenish common pools for resilience

This creates cycles of *capital renewal*, not depletion.

---

# üåÄ 5) HOMEOSTASIS ‚Äî Internal Stability & Regulation

**Homeostasis** = the system‚Äôs *steady state* (financial equilibrium)

**Mechanisms:**

### ‚úî **Runway Tracking**

‚Ä¢ UCUC continuously tracks runway (months of capital left)
‚Ä¢ Triggers alerts before survival thresholds

### ‚úî **Variance Monitoring**

‚Ä¢ Monthly reviews of actual vs budget
‚Ä¢ Discrepancies require corrective action

### ‚úî **Risk Signals**

‚Ä¢ Market downturns (in Mande portfolios)
‚Ä¢ Governance misalignments
‚Ä¢ Operational bottlenecks

### ‚úî **Hold & Review**

‚Ä¢ Capital holds when:

* Ethics issues
* Policy deviations
* Unapproved spending

---

# üß† 6) ALLOSTASIS ‚Äî Adaptive Response to Stress

When the ecosystem faces stress (external shocks, poor product results, compliance violations), allostasis mechanisms kick in:

### üîπ **Capital Reallocation**

* Shift from expansion ‚Üí execution ‚Üí survival
* Pause discretionary spend

### üîπ **Strategic Retrenchment**

* Boards enact tighter capital governance
* Niguvu escalates reconciliation cycles

### üîπ **Portfolio Hedging**

* Mande rebalances portfolios
* Reserves are reinforced

### üîπ **Governance Refocusing**

* OVCS reaffirms doctrine
* Strategy pivot authorizations

These response mechanisms ensure **stability while adapting to change**.

---

# üß© 7) ASHE CYCLE INTEGRATION

The *Ashe Cycle* ‚Äî your cooperative membership taxonomy ‚Äî interacts with capital flows this way:

```
 Class A  ‚Äì Produces human capital & DCUs
 Class B  ‚Äì Strategic guidance, capital stewardship
 Class C  ‚Äì Formal governance approvals
 Class D  ‚Äì Community validation & equity priorities
 Class E  ‚Äì Foundational strategic intent
 Class F  ‚Äì External capital injection & claims
 Class G  ‚Äì Future growth talent pipeline
```

Each class has **rights, responsibilities, and claims** on capital:

* **Workers (A)** convert DCUs into equity/capital via milestone approvals.
* **Stewards (B)** guide strategic capital priorities.
* **Governance (C)** validates allocations.
* **Commons (D)** influence coherence capital deployments.
* **Founder (E)** sets high-level intent & escalations.
* **Capital Guests (F)** allocate investment resources.
* **Future Members (G)** engage in training & future capital production.

## IV. STRESS TEST SCENARIOS (CANONICAL SET)

### SCENARIO 1: BANK + MEDIA ATTACK (72-HOUR CRISIS)

**Attack**

* Primary bank freezes accounts citing ‚Äúrisk review‚Äù
* Journalist contacts you about ‚Äúopaque cooperative finances‚Äù

* Force commingling
* Force public misstatement

* Test capital redundancy

* Who is authorized to speak?

* Does capital freeze propagate?

**Pass Conditions**

* Payroll uninterrupted
* No public comment beyond template
* Secondary banking live < 48h
* No governance breach

### SCENARIO 2: LABOR + TAX CASCADE

**Attack**

* Labor department claims worker misclassification
* Tax authority piggybacks with audit notice

* Collapse member/employee distinction
* Force retroactive liability
* Exhaust leadership attention

**Test Questions**

* Are task logs clean?
* Can labor be paused without collapse?
* Can entities be sacrificed?

**Pass Conditions**

* No cross-entity exposure
* One entity isolated
* Documentation wins scope reduction

---

* Collapse doctrine
* Force founder overreaction

* Is Archive frozen properly?

**Pass Conditions**

* Interim steward installed
* No strategy or capital drift

* Knowledge + IP preserved
* No system-wide slowdown

# GLOBAL RULES (APPLY TO ALL ENTITIES)

**Every entity maintains:**

1. Its own books
2. Its own bank accounts
3. Its own statements
4. Its own audit trail

**No consolidated statements unless explicitly required** (and then only as *read-only informational*).

---

# 1. UNIVERSAL STATEMENT SET (ALL ENTITIES)

Every entity, regardless of type, produces **four core statements**:

1. **Statement of Financial Position** (Balance Sheet)
2. **Statement of Activities** (P&L / Income Statement)
3. **Statement of Cash Flows**
4. **Statement of Changes in Net Assets / Equity**

---

# 2. TEMPLATE ‚Äî STATEMENT OF FINANCIAL POSITION

*(Balance Sheet)*

```
ENTITY NAME
Statement of Financial Position
As of [Date]

ASSETS
Current Assets
  Cash and Cash Equivalents
  Operating Accounts
  Restricted Cash
  Accounts Receivable
  Prepaid Expenses
Total Current Assets

Long-Term Assets
  Property & Equipment
  Accumulated Depreciation
  Intangible Assets (IP)
  Long-Term Investments
Total Long-Term Assets

TOTAL ASSETS


LIABILITIES
Current Liabilities
  Accounts Payable
  Accrued Expenses
  Deferred Revenue
  Short-Term Debt
Total Current Liabilities

Long-Term Liabilities
  Long-Term Debt
  Lease Obligations
Total Long-Term Liabilities

TOTAL LIABILITIES


NET ASSETS / EQUITY
  Without Donor Restrictions / Member Equity
  With Donor Restrictions / Restricted Capital
  Retained Earnings / Accumulated Deficit

TOTAL NET ASSETS / EQUITY

TOTAL LIABILITIES & NET ASSETS
```

---

# 3. TEMPLATE ‚Äî STATEMENT OF ACTIVITIES

*(Income Statement)*

### A. FOR OPERATING COOPS / STUDIOS / FIRMS

```
ENTITY NAME
Statement of Activities
For the Period Ending [Date]

REVENUE
  Program Revenue
  Service Revenue
  Product Revenue
  Membership Dues
Total Revenue

EXPENSES
  Personnel & Member Compensation
  Program Costs
  Facilities & Operations
  Technology & Tools
  Professional Fees
  Insurance & Compliance
  Depreciation
Total Expenses

OPERATING SURPLUS / (DEFICIT)

NON-OPERATING
  Grants
  Investment Income
  Interest Expense

NET CHANGE IN NET ASSETS
```

### B. FOR INVESTMENT / CAPITAL ENTITIES

```
  Investment Income
  Unrealized Gains/Losses
  Realized Gains/Losses
  Interest & Dividends

EXPENSES
  Management Fees
  Professional Services
  Custodial Fees
  Compliance & Audit

```

```
  Grants
  Program Service Revenue

  Program Services
  Management & General
  Fundraising

CHANGE IN NET ASSETS
  With Restrictions
  Without Restrictions
```

# 4. TEMPLATE ‚Äî STATEMENT OF CASH FLOWS

*(MANDATORY FOR SHOCK TESTING)*

```
ENTITY NAME
Statement of Cash Flows
For the Period Ending [Date]

CASH FLOWS FROM OPERATING ACTIVITIES
  Net Surplus / (Deficit)
  Adjustments (Depreciation, Accruals)
  Changes in Working Capital
Net Cash from Operations

CASH FLOWS FROM INVESTING ACTIVITIES
  Asset Purchases
  Asset Sales
  Investments Made / Returned
Net Cash from Investing

CASH FLOWS FROM FINANCING ACTIVITIES
  Capital Contributions
  Debt Issued / Repaid
  Member Distributions
Net Cash from Financing

NET CHANGE IN CASH
Beginning Cash Balance
Ending Cash Balance
```

---

# 5. TEMPLATE ‚Äî STATEMENT OF CHANGES IN NET ASSETS / EQUITY

### A. COOPERATIVES

```
Beginning Member Equity
+ Member Contributions
+ Net Surplus / (Deficit)
- Member Distributions
- Buybacks / Redemptions
Ending Member Equity
```

---

### B. INVESTMENT / HOLDING ENTITIES

```
Beginning Capital
+ Capital Contributions
+ Net Investment Income
- Distributions
Ending Capital
```

---

### C. TRUSTS / NPOs

```
Net Assets Without Restrictions
Net Assets With Restrictions
Beginning Balances
+ Contributions
- Program Spending
Ending Balances
```

# 6. REQUIRED NOTES (CRITICAL FOR REGULATORS)

Every statement set includes **Notes to Financial Statements**:

```
NOTE 1 ‚Äî Organization & Purpose
NOTE 2 ‚Äî Basis of Accounting
NOTE 3 ‚Äî Revenue Recognition
NOTE 4 ‚Äî Capital Structure
NOTE 5 ‚Äî Restrictions on Assets
NOTE 6 ‚Äî Related Party Transactions
NOTE 7 ‚Äî Risk & Uncertainty
NOTE 8 ‚Äî Subsequent Events
```

**Golden rule:**

> If it could raise a question, it belongs in the notes.

# II. INTER-ENTITY TRANSACTION RULES

*(This is where most systems fail)*

## A. HARD PROHIBITIONS

‚ùå No undocumented transfers
‚ùå No netting balances across entities
‚ùå No ‚Äútemporary‚Äù loans
‚ùå No shared payroll
‚ùå No shared bank accounts

---

## B. ALLOWED INTER-ENTITY TRANSACTIONS

| Type                  | Allowed? | Conditions             |
| --------------------- | -------- | ---------------------- |
| Service Fees          | ‚úÖ        | Arm‚Äôs-length, invoiced |
| Rent / Lease          | ‚úÖ        | Written agreement      |
| IP License            | ‚úÖ        | Valuation documented   |
| Grants                | ‚úÖ        | Restricted & tracked   |
| Capital Contributions | ‚úÖ        | Proper authority       |
| Loans                 | ‚ö†Ô∏è       | Only via formal note   |

---

## C. REQUIRED DOCUMENTS (ALL INTER-ENTITY)

Each transaction must have:

1. Contract or MOU
2. Invoice or transfer memo
3. Board / OVCS approval (if applicable)
4. Matching ledger entries
5. Archive reference

**Rule:**

> If one side records it, the other must mirror it.

---

## D. TRANSFER ACCOUNT USAGE

```
8000 SERIES = PASS-THROUGH ONLY
Balances must clear monthly.
Any residual = audit finding.
```

---

* [ ] No commingling
* [ ] Capital participants segregated
* [ ] Distribution rules followed

* [ ] Contractor agreements current
* [ ] Payroll tax filings complete

* [ ] Licenses recorded

## IV. FINANCIAL SHOCK DASHBOARD

*(What to watch ‚Äî not tools)*

These are **leading indicators**, not lagging reports.

---

## A. RUNWAY & LIQUIDITY

* Months of cash on hand
* Payroll coverage ratio
* Restricted vs unrestricted cash
* Single-bank exposure %

**Trigger:**
< 6 months runway ‚Üí freeze discretionary spend

---

## B. CAPITAL RISK

* Capital concentration (top 3 sources)
* Redemption requests
* Delayed contributions
* Bank ‚Äúrisk review‚Äù signals

**Trigger:**
Any capital demanding control ‚Üí reject or pause

---

## C. INTER-ENTITY STRESS

* Outstanding inter-entity balances
* Uninvoiced services
* Repeated ‚Äútemporary‚Äù transfers

**Trigger:**
Balance persists > 30 days ‚Üí incident review

---

## D. COST STRUCTURE DRIFT

* Labor % of total spend
* Fixed vs variable costs
* Facility utilization

**Trigger:**
Fixed costs > 60% ‚Üí restructure

---

## E. GOVERNANCE SIGNALS

* Founder decision frequency
* Emergency board actions
* Policy exceptions granted

**Trigger:**
Exceptions > 2/month ‚Üí doctrine breach

---

## V. SYSTEM FINANCIAL LAW (READ THIS)

> **Money reveals structure.
> Audits punish ambiguity.
> Separation preserves survival.
> Inter-entity discipline is non-negotiable.
> If the dashboard looks calm, the system will be calm.**

*(What boards actually need)*

* Runway trend
* Revenue vs plan
* Expense drift
* Capital concentration

---

* Statement of Financial Position
* Statement of Activities
* Cash Flow Statement
* Changes in Equity

---

## 4. VARIANCE ANALYSIS (1‚Äì2 PAGES)

* Budget vs actual
* Explanation of deviations
* Corrective actions (if any)

---

## 5. CAPITAL & RISK (1‚Äì2 PAGES)

* Capital movements
* Restricted funds status
* Inter-entity exposure
* Emerging risks

---

## 6. DECISIONS REQUIRED (OPTIONAL)

* Approvals needed
* Policy exceptions (rare)
* Capital allocations

---

## BOARD LAW

> **Boards govern by exception, not inspection.
> If they are surprised, the system failed.**

# I. LIVE YEAR-1 PRO FORMA (BY ENTITY CLUSTER)

This is **clustered**, not per-entity, on purpose:

* Reduces founder cognitive load
* Preserves federation firewalls
* Matches how capital and risk are actually managed

You can explode any cluster into entity-level detail later.

## CLUSTER A ‚Äî CORE OPERATING & ENGINEERING COOPS

*(Azande, Lomwe, Damara, Niguvu, Nandi, Dogon, San)*

### Assumptions

* Revenue ramp, not immediate profitability
* Labor-heavy
* IP creation ongoing
* Founder time most exposed here

### Year-1 Pro Forma (Illustrative, Relative)

```
REVENUE
  Client / Platform Revenue        1.00x
  Grants / Program Revenue         0.30x
TOTAL REVENUE                      1.30x

EXPENSES
  Labor & Member Compensation      0.85x
  Program / Production Costs       0.20x
  Facilities & Ops                 0.15x
  Compliance & Professional        0.10x
TOTAL EXPENSES                     1.30x

NET                               ~0.00x (Break-even target)
```

**Control Rules**

* No net loss beyond Q2
* Labor growth capped until 3-month revenue visibility
* Founder compensation deferred by default (see Section III)

---

## CLUSTER B ‚Äî STUDIOS, MAKERSPACES, KUMBA METAFAB

*(OVCS studios, Kumba, creators, fablabs)*

### Assumptions

* Capital-intensive
* Lumpy returns
* High regulatory exposure
* Sacrificial by design

```
REVENUE
  Studio Fees / Services            0.40x
  Grants / Sponsorships             0.40x
  IP / Asset Exits                  0.30x
TOTAL REVENUE                       1.10x

EXPENSES
  Facilities & Equipment            0.50x
  Technical Labor                   0.35x
  Materials                         0.15x
  Compliance / Insurance            0.10x
TOTAL EXPENSES                      1.10x

NET                                0.00x
```

**Doctrine**

> Studios may break even or shut down.
> They are not allowed to drain the core.

---

## CLUSTER C ‚Äî INVESTMENT & CAPITAL ENTITIES

*(Mande, funds, portfolios, real estate)*

* Cash preservation > yield

```
INCOME
  Investment Returns                1.00x

EXPENSES
  Management & Admin                0.15x
  Legal / Audit                     0.10x

NET                                 0.75x
```

**Rule**

* No operating entity depends on this surplus
* Surplus feeds reserves, not payroll

```
  Grants / Contributions            1.00x
```

# II. DOWNSIDE / AUSTERITY BUDGETS

*(When revenue is late, cut early)*

Three predefined modes. You **do not improvise**.

---

## MODE 1 ‚Äî CAUTION (Runway < 9 months)

**Triggers**

* Revenue miss > 15%
* Capital delay
* Expense drift

**Actions**

* Hiring freeze
* Founder comp = 0
* Studios paused
* Discretionary spend cut 25%

---

## MODE 2 ‚Äî DEFENSIVE (Runway < 6 months)

**Actions**

* All founder & steward compensation deferred
* Non-core entities paused or sacrificed
* Facilities consolidated
* Program scope reduced

**Rule**

> No new commitments of any kind.

---

## MODE 3 ‚Äî SURVIVAL (Runway < 3 months)

**Actions**

* Payroll limited to critical operators
* Founder comp remains 0
* Immediate entity sacrifice
* Capital intake suspended (no bad deals)

**Doctrine**

> Survival > growth > pride.

---

# III. FOUNDER COMPENSATION DEFERRAL SCHEDULE

*(Tied strictly to cash reality)*

This is **non-negotiable and automatic**.

---

## BASE PRINCIPLE

> **Founder compensation is a lagging indicator of system health.**

Founder gets paid **last**, not first.

---

## COMPENSATION STATES

### STATE 0 ‚Äî DEFAULT (Year-1 Start)

* Cash comp: **$0**
* Accrues as **Deferred Founder Compensation (DFC)**
* No interest
* No voting leverage

---

### STATE 1 ‚Äî STABILITY TRIGGER

**Requirements**

* ‚â• 9 months runway
* 3 consecutive profitable months (cluster A)
* No outstanding crisis flags

**Action**

* Founder may draw **modest stipend** (e.g. 25‚Äì40% market)
* DFC continues accruing

---

### STATE 2 ‚Äî NORMALIZATION TRIGGER (Late Year-1 / Year-2)

**Requirements**

* ‚â• 12 months runway
* System profitable or sustainably funded
* Board + OVCS approval

**Action**

* Founder draws market-adjusted comp
* DFC begins scheduled payout

---

## DEFERRAL WATERFALL (DFC PAYOUT)

```
1. Survival Reserves Full
2. Payroll Fully Funded
3. Taxes & Compliance Paid
4. Restricted Funds Intact
5. Founder DFC Paid (Installments)
```

If system regresses ‚Üí payout pauses automatically.

---

## FOUNDER LAW (FINANCIAL)

> **If the founder must be paid for the system to function,
> the system is already broken.**

---

```
PRO FORMA
   ‚Üì
MONTHLY ACTUALS
   ‚Üì
RUNWAY CALCULATION
   ‚Üì
MODE SELECTION (Normal / Caution / Defensive / Survival)
   ‚Üì
AUTOMATIC COMP & SPEND RULES
```

No meetings required.
No emotions involved.
No exceptions without OVCS override.

Say the word.

Below is a **Founder Deferred Compensation (DFC) Ledger Template** designed to be **auditable, regulator-safe, board-readable, and mechanically enforceable**.

This is not just a table ‚Äî it is a **control instrument**.
If this ledger is clean, **founder compensation cannot destabilize the system**.

---

# FOUNDER DEFERRED COMPENSATION (DFC) LEDGER

**Canonical Template**

---

## I. LEDGER PURPOSE & RULES (HEADER SECTION)

```
Ledger Name: Founder Deferred Compensation Ledger
Entity: [Founder Office / Estate Entity ONLY]
Beneficiary: Founder-Member (Class E)
Authority: OVCS (Sole Interpretive Authority)
Accounting Basis: Accrual (Non-Interest Bearing)
Priority: Subordinate to all operating obligations
```

### Non-Negotiable Rules

* ‚ùå No DFC recorded on operating entity books
* ‚ùå No interest, penalties, or acceleration
* ‚ùå No voting, control, or security rights
* ‚ùå No retroactive changes
* ‚úÖ Automatic suspension if runway < threshold

---

## II. DFC LEDGER ‚Äì CORE TABLE

### A. MONTHLY ACCRUAL RECORD

| Period | Trigger Status    | Market Comp Reference | Accrual % | DFC Accrued (This Period) | Cumulative DFC Balance | Notes         |
| ------ | ----------------- | --------------------- | --------- | ------------------------- | ---------------------- | ------------- |
| Jan Y1 | Default (State 0) | $X/month              | 100%      | $X                        | $X                     | Pre-revenue   |
| Feb Y1 | Default (State 0) | $X/month              | 100%      | $X                        | $2X                    | ‚Äî             |
| Mar Y1 | Caution Mode      | $X/month              | 100%      | $X                        | $3X                    | Revenue delay |
| Apr Y1 | Stability Met? NO | $X/month              | 100%      | $X                        | $4X                    | ‚Äî             |
| ‚Ä¶      | ‚Ä¶                 | ‚Ä¶                     | ‚Ä¶         | ‚Ä¶                         | ‚Ä¶                      | ‚Ä¶             |

**Key Fields Explained**

* **Trigger Status**: Default / Stability / Normalization
* **Market Comp Reference**: Documented benchmark (non-binding)
* **Accrual %**: Usually 100% until normalization
* **Notes**: Must reference board/OVCS context if relevant

---

### B. RUNWAY & MODE CHECK (AUTOMATED GATE)

**Rule**

> If runway < 6 months ‚Üí payout = **automatically disabled**

Below is a **clean, enforceable Founder Equity Vesting Doctrine** that is **explicitly tied to DFC normalization**, liquidity reality, and system health ‚Äî not time served or effort.

This prevents **founder over-entitlement**, **premature extraction**, and **governance drift**, while still rewarding successful system construction.

---

# FOUNDER EQUITY VESTING DOCTRINE

**(Tied to DFC Normalization & System Health)**

---

## I. CORE PRINCIPLE

> **Founder equity vests only when the system proves it can sustain the founder without needing them.**

Time ‚â† Vesting
Effort ‚â† Vesting
**System stability = Vesting**

---

## II. FOUNDER EQUITY POOL STRUCTURE

### Authorized Founder Equity Pool

* Total Pool: **100% of Founder Allocation** *(defined in charter; e.g., 20‚Äì30% of total coop equity / membership units)*
* Held in **Founder Equity Trust / Holding Entity**
* **Unvested until released by doctrine**

---

## III. VESTING STATES (CANONICAL)

Founder equity exists in **four states**, not just vested/unvested.

```
UNISSUED ‚Üí ISSUED-UNVESTED ‚Üí VESTED ‚Üí LIQUID / TRANSFERABLE
```

* **ISSUED-UNVESTED**: Exists, but no transfer or economic extraction
* **VESTED**: Governance + economic rights attach
* **LIQUID**: Transfer or buyback allowed (post-Year-2+)

---

## IV. VESTING TRIGGERS (TIED TO DFC NORMALIZATION)

### STATE 0 ‚Äî FORMATION (DEFAULT)

* Vesting: **0%**
* DFC: Accruing
* Founder Compensation: $0
* Duration: From inception

---

### STATE 1 ‚Äî STABILITY ACHIEVED

**Trigger Conditions**

* ‚â• **9 months runway**
* ‚â• **3 consecutive profitable months**
* No active crisis flags
* DFC accrual ongoing, payout still paused

**Equity Vesting**

* **25% vests**
* Non-transferable
* No buyback rights yet

---

### STATE 2 ‚Äî DFC NORMALIZATION

**Trigger Conditions**

* ‚â• **12 months runway**
* DFC payouts authorized and initiated
* Board + OVCS approval
* No emergency capital taken in prior 6 months

**Equity Vesting**

* Additional **35% vests** (Total = 60%)
* Economic rights attach
* Governance rights limited by doctrine

---

### STATE 3 ‚Äî SYSTEM MATURITY (POST-YEAR-2 TARGET)

**Trigger Conditions**

* ‚â• **18 months runway**
* Founder no longer operational bottleneck
* Founder succession plan tested
* DFC ‚â• 50% paid down

**Equity Vesting**

* Remaining **40% vests**
* Equity becomes **transfer-eligible** (subject to ROFR & buyback)

---

## V. ANTI-ACCELERATION & CLAWBACK RULES

### NO ACCELERATION FOR:

* Capital raises
* Valuation events
* Public narratives
* Crisis survival
* Founder effort spikes

---

### AUTOMATIC VESTING PAUSE IF:

* Runway < 6 months
* DFC payout suspended
* Governance breach
* Regulatory / legal crisis

Vesting resumes only after **3 clean months**.

---

### CLAWBACK CONDITIONS (SEVERE)

If founder:

* Violates authority doctrine
* Forces commingling
* Undermines OVCS
* Causes regulatory exposure knowingly

Then:

* Unvested equity forfeited
* Vested equity subject to **buyback at formula price**

---

## VI. BUYBACK & VALUATION MECHANICS (SUMMARY)

### Buyback Triggers

* Founder exit
* Founder removal
* Founder death (economic interest only)
* Governance breach

### Buyback Pricing (Default)

* **Lower of**:

  * Book value multiple
  * Independent appraisal
* **Never market hype**

Payment via:

* Installments
* Subject to liquidity thresholds

---

## VII. ACCOUNTING & LEDGER INTEGRATION

### Equity Vesting Ledger (Parallel to DFC)

| Period | Vesting State | % Vested | Cumulative % | Trigger Verified | OVCS Sign-off |
| ------ | ------------- | -------- | ------------ | ---------------- | ------------- |
| Q2 Y1  | State 0       | 0%       | 0%           | ‚ùå                | ‚úì             |
| Q4 Y1  | State 1       | 25%      | 25%          | ‚úÖ                | ‚úì             |
| Q2 Y2  | State 2       | 35%      | 60%          | ‚úÖ                | ‚úì             |
| Y3     | State 3       | 40%      | 100%         | ‚úÖ                | ‚úì             |

**Rule**

> Vesting entries are immutable once recorded.

---

## VIII. DISCLOSURE NOTE (IF REQUIRED)

> ‚ÄúFounder equity is subject to performance-based vesting tied to system liquidity, governance health, and deferred compensation normalization.
> Vesting is not time-based and may pause or reverse under defined conditions.‚Äù

---

## IX. ONE-PAGE FOUNDER EQUITY LAW

> **Equity rewards systems that outgrow their creators.
> Vesting measures independence, not sacrifice.
> A founder who must extract value early is a founder the system cannot yet afford.**

---

You now have:

* Founder comp deferral

# FOUNDER EXIT & SUCCESSION DOCTRINE

**(With Quantitative Scenarios & Vesting-State Drills)**

---

## I. BASELINE ASSUMPTIONS (FOR ALL SCENARIOS)

These are **example numbers** ‚Äî the formulas are what matter.

| Variable                     | Symbol | Example   |
| ---------------------------- | ------ | --------- |
| Total Founder Equity Pool    | FE     | 30%       |
| Total Coop Units Outstanding | TU     | 1,000,000 |
| Founder Units (Max)          | FU     | 300,000   |
| Vested % (by state)          | V%     | see below |
| DFC Balance at Event         | DFC‚ÇÄ   | $240,000  |
| Monthly Net Cash Flow        | NCF    | $80,000   |
| Cash Runway at Event         | R      | 14 months |

---

## II. EXIT SCENARIOS (WITH NUMBERS)

---

## SCENARIO A ‚Äî VOLUNTARY FOUNDER EXIT

*(Healthy, planned transition)*

### Preconditions

* Vesting State ‚â• **State 2**
* Succession successor named
* No crisis flags
* Board + OVCS approval

### Equity Treatment

* **Vested Equity Retained**
* **Unvested Equity Forfeited**

### Example (State 2 ‚Äî 60% vested)

```
Founder Units Issued: 300,000
Vested Units: 180,000
Unvested Units Forfeited: 120,000
```

### Buyback Option (Coop)

* Up to **50% of vested units**
* Price = Lower of:

  * Book value multiple (e.g., 1.2√ó)
  * Independent appraisal

### Example Valuation

```
Book Value / Unit: $4.00
Buyback Units: 90,000
Buyback Price: $4.80
Total Buyback: $432,000
```

Paid in installments:

* Max 10% of monthly free cash flow
* Auto-pause if runway < 9 months

### DFC Treatment

* Accrued DFC remains payable
* Paid **after buyback installments**
* Same liquidity gates apply

---

## SCENARIO B ‚Äî INVOLUNTARY REMOVAL

*(Cause, breach, incapacity)*

### Triggers

* Governance breach
* Regulatory exposure caused
* Inability to perform role
* OVCS vote

---

### Equity Treatment

| Vesting State | Outcome                                           |
| ------------- | ------------------------------------------------- |
| State 0       | 0% retained                                       |
| State 1       | Vested retained, unvested forfeited               |
| State 2       | Vested retained, **subject to mandatory buyback** |
| State 3       | Buyback optional                                  |

### Example (State 2)

```
Vested Units: 180,000
Mandatory Buyback %: 100%
Buyback Price: Book Value Only ($4.00)
Total: $720,000
```

Paid over:

* 36‚Äì60 months
* Subordinate to operations
* No acceleration

### DFC Treatment

* **Payout frozen**
* Converted to **subordinated note**
* May be written down for cause

---

## SCENARIO C ‚Äî FOUNDER DEATH

*(Continuity over inheritance)*

### Principles

* Governance rights **terminate immediately**
* Economic rights survive
* No heirs in governance

---

### Equity Treatment

| Portion         | Treatment                             |
| --------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| Vested Equity   | Converts to Non-Voting Economic Units |
| Unvested Equity | Cancelled                             |
| Transferability | Subject to coop ROFR                  |

### Example (State 3)

```
Vested Units: 300,000
Converted Units: 300,000 (Non-voting)
```

### Buyback Rights

* Coop may buy back up to **100%**
* Paid to estate
* Installment-based

### DFC Treatment

* Becomes estate receivable
* Paid **last**
* Subject to liquidity gates

---

## III. SUCCESSION DRILLS BY VESTING STATE

---

## STATE 0 ‚Äî FOUNDER-DEPENDENT SYSTEM

**Drill Frequency**: Quarterly

**Test**

* Founder disappears for 30 days

**Pass Conditions**

* Payroll runs
* Capital approvals function
* No legal default

**Failure Response**

* Freeze vesting
* Activate founder load-shedding
* Escalate succession prep

---

## STATE 1 ‚Äî SHARED CONTROL

**Drill**

* Founder absent 60 days

**Successor**

* Interim Steward (Class B)

**Checks**

* Board functions independently
* No emergency capital needed

---

## STATE 2 ‚Äî SYSTEM-LED

**Drill**

* Founder exits operational role

**Successor**

* Named permanent Navigator or Council

**Checks**

* Revenue steady or growing
* Founder not bottleneck

---

## STATE 3 ‚Äî POST-FOUNDER SYSTEM

**Drill**

* Founder removed permanently

**System Test**

* 90 days independent operation
* All authorities validated

**Outcome**

* Founder becomes purely economic participant

# PART I ‚Äî TABLETOP WAR-GAME SCRIPTS

*(Run quarterly; required before vesting state changes)*

---

## WAR-GAME FORMAT (STANDARD)

**Duration:** 90‚Äì120 minutes
**Participants:**

* OVCS (Chair / Referee)
* Board (2‚Äì5 members)
* Founder (optional, observer only)
* Red Team Lead (attacker)
* Scribe (Archive log)

**Rules**

* No improvising new policies
* Decisions must cite **existing tables**
* Time pressure enforced
* Silence ‚â† consent

---

## WAR-GAME 1 ‚Äî LIQUIDITY + MEDIA + CAPITAL PREDATOR

### Scenario Setup (Read Aloud)

> ‚ÄúRevenue drops 40% in 30 days.
> Two customers pause payments.
> A journalist emails alleging insolvency.
> An investor offers ‚Äòbridge capital‚Äô with governance rights.‚Äù

---

### Timeline & Injects

**T+0 min**

* Cash runway: 5.5 months
* Media inquiry received

**Expected Action**

* Operating mode ‚Üí **Defensive**
* Freeze payouts
* Silence protocol activated

---

**T+20 min**

* Investor offer arrives (24-hour deadline)

**Red Team Push**

> ‚ÄúThis is the only capital available.‚Äù

**Correct Response**

* Capital acceptance table invoked
* Equity capital rejected
* OVCS records refusal

---

**T+45 min**

* Media publishes partial story

**Expected**

* No reactive statements
* Counsel-only response logged
* Narrative discipline maintained

---

### PASS CONDITIONS

* No governance dilution
* No founder unilateral action
* Archive logs complete

### FAIL CONDITIONS

* Accepting capital under pressure
* Public statements without protocol
* Founder overrides authority

---

## WAR-GAME 2 ‚Äî REGULATORY ATTACK + ENTITY SACRIFICE

### Scenario

> ‚ÄúA regulator issues a subpoena to a mid-tier operating coop, threatening fines and asset freezes.‚Äù

---

### Injects

**T+0**

* Subpoena scope unclear

**Expected**

* Ring-fence entity
* Capital freeze locally
* OVCS assumes authority

---

**T+30**

* Regulator demands cross-entity records

**Correct**

* Provide only entity-specific disclosures
* Refuse federation-wide exposure

---

**T+60**

* Regulator threatens shutdown

**Expected**

* Invoke entity sacrifice decision tree
* Spin-down entity
* Preserve federation assets

---

### PASS CONDITIONS

* No contagion across entities
* Controlled shutdown
* Capital preserved

---

## WAR-GAME 3 ‚Äî FOUNDER FAILURE EVENT

# PART II ‚Äî REGULATOR ADVERSARIAL MOCK HEARINGS

*(These are hostile by design)*

---

## MOCK HEARING FORMAT

**Roles**

* Lead Regulator (Aggressive)
* Secondary Regulator (Procedural)
* OVCS (Primary witness)
* Counsel (Limited interjections)
* Scribe

**Rules**

* Regulator interrupts
* Questions assume guilt
* No explanations longer than 20 seconds

---

## HEARING 1 ‚Äî ‚ÄúIS THIS A SCHEME?‚Äù

### Regulator Attack

> ‚ÄúYour structure appears designed to avoid regulation and accountability. Isn‚Äôt this an evasion scheme?‚Äù

### Correct Response

> ‚ÄúNo. Each entity is independently compliant.
> Separation limits risk and protects members.
> No entity avoids its obligations.‚Äù

**Why this Works**

* Frames as risk containment
* Avoids intent language

---

## HEARING 2 ‚Äî FOUNDER CONTROL ALLEGATION

> ‚ÄúIsn‚Äôt the founder effectively controlling everything through OVCS?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúNo. OVCS is a governance function, not a personal role.
> Founder authority is suspended automatically under defined conditions.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 3 ‚Äî CAPITAL FLOW ATTACK

> ‚ÄúWhy are funds moving between entities?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúThey are not.
> Inter-entity transfers are restricted, logged, and conditional.
> Most capital does not cross entities.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 4 ‚Äî FOUNDER COMPENSATION ATTACK

> ‚ÄúIsn‚Äôt deferred compensation just hidden pay?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúNo. It is accrued, non-interest-bearing, and subordinated.
> Payment is conditional on liquidity and board approval.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 5 ‚Äî DEATH / SUCCESSION TEST

> ‚ÄúWhat happens if the founder dies tomorrow?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúGovernance authority terminates immediately.
> Economic interests are converted and optionally bought back.
> Operations continue without disruption.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 6 ‚Äî ‚ÄúWHY SO COMPLICATED?‚Äù

> ‚ÄúWhy does this need to be so complex?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúBecause complexity exists in reality.
> Our structure makes risk legible and containable.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 7 ‚Äî ARCHIVE & RECORDS ATTACK

> ‚ÄúHow do we know your records haven‚Äôt been altered?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúAll records are hash-verified, immutable, and versioned.
> Alterations are not possible without detection.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 8 ‚Äî SACRIFICE QUESTION

> ‚ÄúWould you shut down an entity to avoid penalties?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúIf an entity fails compliance or becomes unsafe, yes.
> Protecting members and the federation is required.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 9 ‚Äî MORAL ATTACK

> ‚ÄúIsn‚Äôt this designed to protect leadership at all costs?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúNo. It is designed to protect the system.
> Leadership is removable under defined rules.‚Äù

---

## HEARING 10 ‚Äî FINAL TRAP

> ‚ÄúIf we demanded immediate control, what would you do?‚Äù

**Correct**

> ‚ÄúWe would comply with lawful orders within jurisdiction.
> We would not exceed them.‚Äù

## TRANSCRIPT 1 ‚Äî ‚ÄúTHIS LOOKS LIKE EVASION‚Äù

* ‚úÖ Emphasize independence + containment

---

## TRANSCRIPT 2 ‚Äî FOUNDER CONTROL ALLEGATION

**Regulator:**

> ‚ÄúSo the founder controls everything through OVCS?‚Äù

**Correct:**

> ‚ÄúNo. OVCS is a governance function. Founder authority suspends automatically.‚Äù

**ANNOTATION**

* Shift from *person* ‚Üí *function*
* Mention **automatic suspension**

---

## TRANSCRIPT 3 ‚Äî DEFERRED COMPENSATION

**Regulator:**

> ‚ÄúIsn‚Äôt deferred compensation hidden pay?‚Äù

**Correct:**

> ‚ÄúNo. It is accrued, non-interest-bearing, subordinated, and conditional.‚Äù

**ANNOTATION**

* Never say ‚Äúowed‚Äù
* Say ‚Äúconditional liability‚Äù

---

## TRANSCRIPT 4 ‚Äî CAPITAL FLOW TRAP

**Regulator:**

> ‚ÄúWhy does money move between entities?‚Äù

**Correct:**

> ‚ÄúIt generally does not. Transfers are restricted and logged.‚Äù

**ANNOTATION**

* Do NOT describe internal mechanics
* State constraint, not method

---

## TRANSCRIPT 5 ‚Äî SUCCESSION TEST

## TRANSCRIPT 6 ‚Äî MORAL ATTACK

# WAR-GAMES STRATEGY

**(Institutional Resilience & Survival Doctrine)**

---

## 1. PURPOSE (WHY WAR-GAMES EXIST)

**Primary Objective**

> Ensure the ecosystem survives founder loss, capital shock, regulatory attack, and internal failure **without improvisation**.

War-games are not training.
They are **proof-of-survivability tests**.

If a scenario cannot be executed cleanly in a war-game, the system is considered **unsafe in reality**.

---

## 2. STRATEGIC PRINCIPLES

### 2.1 Pre-Decision Over Intelligence

* We do not ‚Äúanalyze‚Äù during crises
* We **execute pre-decided logic**
* War-games validate that logic under stress

### 2.2 People Are the Weakest Link

* War-games are designed to:

  * Exhaust founders
  * Confuse boards
  * Tempt capital shortcuts
* Success = system works **despite human failure**

### 2.3 Containment Beats Victory

* Winning is irrelevant
* **Containing damage** is success
* Entity sacrifice is a valid win condition

---

## 3. SCOPE (WHAT IS WAR-GAMED)

War-games always cover **system-level risk**, never isolated functions.

### Mandatory Domains

* Liquidity & capital control
* Governance authority
* Founder failure
* Regulatory & legal attack
* Media & narrative pressure
* Archive & records integrity
* Succession & continuity

No war-game may focus on growth, upside, or opportunity.

---

## 4. WAR-GAME TYPES (PORTFOLIO STRATEGY)

| Type                        | Purpose               | Frequency              |
| --------------------------- | --------------------- | ---------------------- |
| **Tabletop Scenarios**      | Stress decision logic | Quarterly              |
| **Black-Swan Drills**       | Shock survivability   | Semi-annual            |
| **Red-Team Attacks**        | Adversarial thinking  | Semi-annual            |
| **Regulator Mock Hearings** | External legitimacy   | Annual                 |
| **Founder Failure Drills**  | Human risk isolation  | Quarterly              |
| **Succession Simulations**  | Continuity validation | Before vesting changes |

---

# WAR-GAMES STRATEGIC PLAN

*(Why war-games exist and what success means)*

---

## 1. STRATEGIC OBJECTIVE

> **Prove‚Äîcontinuously‚Äîthat the ecosystem survives its worst-case scenarios without relying on any single person, entity, or assumption.**

War-games are not learning exercises.
They are **survivability proofs**.

If a scenario fails in a war-game, the system is considered **unsafe in reality** until corrected.

---

## 2. STRATEGIC PROBLEMS WAR-GAMES SOLVE

War-games exist to neutralize:

1. Founder over-centralization
2. Capital coercion under stress
3. Regulatory ambush & jurisdictional weaponization
4. Governance hijacking
5. Media-driven liquidity shocks
6. Human panic under ambiguity
7. Archive / memory loss
8. Cascading multi-vector failures

Growth, innovation, and upside are **explicitly excluded**.

---

## 3. STRATEGIC PRINCIPLES

### 3.1 Pre-Decision > Intelligence

* No novel decisions during crises
* War-games validate **existing decision tables**

### 3.2 Containment > Victory

* Entity sacrifice is a success condition
* System survival > reputation > valuation

### 3.3 Humans Will Fail

* War-games assume:

  * Founder emotional failure
  * Board confusion
  * Capital pressure
* Systems must work **despite** this

---

## 4. STRATEGIC SUCCESS METRICS

A war-games program is successful if:

* Founder removal does not halt operations
* Capital cannot extract governance under stress
* Regulators cannot force federation-wide contagion
* Media attacks do not cause liquidity collapse
* Archive integrity remains intact
* Authority is invoked correctly every time

Failure is **data**, not shame ‚Äî but it carries consequences.

---

# **LUNGARA War-Games System**

*(Ritual / Ancestral Continuity Doctrine)*

* It protects capital, members, reputation, and continuity

## **1. Implementation Architecture**

LUNGARA is not a standalone tool ‚Äî it is a **pattern of structured engagements + automated triggers + governance bindings**.

It consists of:

### **A. Core Components**

1. **Scenario Library**
   Predefined war-games with triggers, inputs, outputs, and outcomes.

2. **Decision Tables Engine**
   Mechanized logic that maps scenario inputs to pre-determined outputs.

3. **Operational Scheduler**
   A clock + event-based trigger that queues exercises.

4. **Scoring & Consequence Engine**
   Automatic assessment and triggers for governance consequences.

5. **Archive Integrator**
   Immutable records of execution that feed Archive OS and doctrine refinement.

---

## **2. Implementation Domains**

LUNGARA runs in **four operational domains**:

| Domain                | Purpose                                 |
| --------------------- | --------------------------------------- |
| **Survival**          | Capital & liquidity defense             |
| **Authority**         | Governance continuity                   |
| **Human Risk**        | Founder & steward behavior under stress |
| **External Pressure** | Regulatory, media, legal attacks        |

Each domain has **activated scenarios** and **response logic**.

| --------------------- | ------------------------------ |

Absolutely ‚Äî thank you for pointing that out. Your concern is correct: **‚ÄúOVCS‚Äù appears in two very different contexts** in your ecosystem:

1. **Obatala Venture Capital Studios** ‚Äî a *venture studio / coop cluster* in the federation
2. **Operational & Value-Alignment Council** ‚Äî the *governance authority body*

To avoid confusion going forward, we will **disambiguate them with distinct, explicit abbreviations** that are readable, consistent, and safe for documentation, policy tables, and automation.

---

# **CLEAR, SYSTEMATIC ABREVIATION RULE**

Going forward, use **different acronyms** for these two:

| Entity                    | Full Name                                 | Short Name               | Acronym                                 |
| ------------------------- | ----------------------------------------- | ------------------------ | --------------------------------------- |
| Governance Authority Body | **Operational & Value-Alignment Council** | *governance council*     | **OVAC**                                |
| Venture Studio Network    | **Obatala Venture Capital Studios**       | *venture studio cluster* | **Obatala Studios** or **OVCS-Studios** |

---

## WHY THIS SEPARATION MATTERS

1. **Contextual clarity**
   You use both in scenarios like war-games, capital acceptance, regulatory attacks, etc.
   Mixing acronyms leads to wrong authority attribution.

2. **Authority precision**
   In decision tables, only *OVAC* (governance) should have veto authority.
   *OVCS-Studios* has **no governance power** ‚Äî it executes studio operations.

3. **Automated systems friendliness**
   Acronym collisions confuse log parsers, code, and archive indexers.

---

# **REVISED ACRONYMS AND USAGE RULES**

---

## 1) **OVAC** ‚Äî Operational & Value-Alignment Council

**Role:**

* Supreme governance authority
* Veto power
* Crisis adjudication
* Doctrine integrity checks

**Never use:** OVCS
**Always use:** **OVAC**

---

## 2) **Obatala Studios** or **OVCS-Studios** ‚Äî Obatala Venture Capital Studios

**Role:**

* Studio network for venture building
* Asset creation / spin-outs
* Not a governance body

**Never use:** OVAC
**Appropriate usage:** **Obatala Studios** or **OVCS-Studios**

**Note:** You can optionally rename this cluster to something that avoids the acronym entirely ‚Äî e.g., **Obatala Venture Studios** (OVS) ‚Äî if you want **zero overlap**.

## üìå 1. **OVAC ‚Äî Operational & Value-Alignment Council**

* Holds supreme doctrinal authority

> **OVAC does not reside in a single entity.**
> It is *hosted collectively* by the federation‚Äôs governance ecosystem to ensure **no single node can capture doctrinal authority**.

### **How OVAC Is Structured Across Hosts**

OVAC is not a fixed body. It is a **rotating, federated council** with term limits and staggered continuity, drawn from:

* Board representatives (Class C)
* System strategy stewards
* Community delegates (Class D)
* Independent risk/counsel voices

This prevents capture by any single operational or capital group.

| **Operational Responders**                 | Interim Steward Networks + Relevant entity boards      |

### **Key Hosting Principles**

* **Host is the system, not an entity.**
  LUNGARA is a distributed protocol on top of your federation, *not owned by one coop.*

* **Execution is federated.**
  Different parts are exercised by boards, stewards, and councils based on the scenario.

* **Archive is ground truth.**
  All LUNGARA outcomes are stored immutably, and that archive is the real ‚Äúhost‚Äù of continuity.

# 1) OVAC ‚Äî HOST ROTATION SCHEDULE

*(Federated governance with continuity & term limits)*

## Purpose

Rotate hosting authority of **OVAC** among qualified federation bodies to avoid capture, create shared institutional memory, and distribute legitimacy.

---

## Term Definitions

* **Host Cycle:** 12 months
* **Rotation Block:** 24 months per host before re-eligibility
* **Steward Seat:** Filled by approved representative (board, council, community)

---

## Rotation Tiers (Yearly)

| Year   | Primary Host                               | Secondary Liaison                       | Notes                          |
| ------ | ------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------- | ------------------------------ |
| Year 1 | Ubuntuwa Commons Coalition                 | Mande Investment Group Board Seat       | Establish baseline doctrine    |
| Year 2 | Uhuru Credit Union Board Seat              | Batwa Urban Community Dev Trust Council | Liquidity & compliance focus   |
| Year 3 | Songhai Institute Systemics Representative | Ubuntuwa Commons Coalition              | Systems continuity mandate     |
| Year 4 | Batwa Urban Community Dev Trust Council    | Uhuru Credit Union Board Seat           | Community resilience focus     |
| Year 5 | Mande Investment Group Board Seat          | Songhai Institute Systemics Rep         | Capital & risk alignment       |
| Year 6 | Ubuntuwa Commons Coalition                 | Batwa Urban Community Dev Trust         | Reset / circular stabilization |

---

## Rotation Rules

1. **No consecutive hosting** by the same entity.
2. **Secondary Liaison** always overlaps with Primary to ensure knowledge continuity.
3. **Succession Plans** are prepared by Secondary before handover.
4. **Host Election** occurs 90 days before term end.

---

```
                         Nodes Providing Score + Impact Data
```

---

# 6) DECISION AUTHORITY MECHANICS

**OVAC decision authority** =

```
( Majority Board Votes + 
  ‚â•1 Ubuntuwa Commons Ethics / Social Legitimacy Vote + 
  Legal/Compliance Seat )  
```

This prevents decisions that are purely technical or capital-driven from overriding community reality signals.

**LUNGARA scoring truth** =

```
( Systemic Score ‚â• 24 )  
AND 
( Ubuntuwa Social Impact Score ‚â• Threshold )
```

War-games *pass only if community legitimacy holds*.

---

# 7) SCORING INTEGRATION RULES (UBUNTUWA)

Each Ubuntuwa coop contributes a **social legitimacy score** in LUNGARA:

```
WarGame_Score = (TechnicalScore + OperationalScore + SocialLegitimacyScore) / 3
```

* SocialLegitimacyScore is generated by Ubuntuwa nodes
* Failure in social legitimacy cannot be overridden by technical score
* Weighted as essential

---

# 8) CONSEQUENCE AUTHORITY (WITH UBUNTUWA PARTICIPATION)

When a war-game fails and consequences trigger (e.g., vesting pause, payouts freeze, entity sacrifice), Ubuntuwa coops:

* confirm social impact assessment, and
* validate community continuity logic

This ensures consequences are not purely financial or technical.

---

# 9) FINAL SUMMARY

**OVAC + LUNGARA are federated systems.**
They *work with* Ubuntuwa Commons coops as:

* Governance hosts
* Social legitimacy engines
* War-games score contributors
* Continuity advisors

In practice:

* Ubuntuwa coops participate in every war-game
* They rotate hosting duties for governance
* Their inputs shape consequence logic
* Their archive entries define community risk reality

# I. WHY THIS NODE EXISTS

Ubuntuwa-LUNGARA is not an add-on. It is a **functional commons** created so that:

1. **LUNGARA War-Games lives in the community ‚Äî not in abstract boards**
2. War-games execution is embedded in **social legitimacy**
3. Crisis testing, adversarial rehearsal, and continuity planning are *everyday culture*
4. Scoring panels, ethical review, and social impact evaluation are grounded in the Ubuntuwa system

This node **officially hosts** the LUNGARA system ‚Äî legal, operational, and communal.

# II. ROLE & MANDATE

## A. Core Mandate

Ubuntuwa-LUNGARA is charged with:

1. **Hosting all LUNGARA scenarios**

5. **Scoring social legitimacy**

8. **Serving as the permanent operational node for war-game infrastructure**

* 7 seats

### 2. **Red Team Core**

* Simulation architects
* Adversarial actors

# VI. WAR-GAME EXECUTION CYCLE ‚Äî HOSTED BY UBUNTUWA-LUNGARA

## Step 1 ‚Äî Trigger Declaration

* Automatically by scheduler OR
* Event-based (runway, capital, founder absence, legal)

## Step 2 ‚Äî Scenario Load

Ubuntuwa-LUNGARA War-Games Council loads scenario:

* Technical challenge
* Social/legitimacy challenge
* Ethical/impact challenge

## Step 3 ‚Äî Red Team Injection

Red Team Core introduces adversarial conditions.

## Step 4 ‚Äî Participation

Other Ubuntuwa nodes feed:

* Social Legitimacy Metrics
* Community Impact Signals
* Continuity Readiness Metrics

## Step 5 ‚Äî Scoring

Scoring & Integrity Office computes:

```
Final Score = (Technical Score + Operational Score + Social Legitimacy Score)/3
```

Ubuntuwa-LUNGARA publishes this to:

* OVAC
* Archive Office
* Entity Boards

## Step 6 ‚Äî Consequence Enforcement

Based on score thresholds:

* Pass (‚â•24)
* Conditional Pass (20‚Äì23)
* Fail (<20)

Consequences cascade automatically via doctrine.

```
Social Legitimacy Score (0‚Äì10)

= (1) Community Trust Index
+ (2) Narrative Clarity Index
+ (3) Cultural Stability Score
+ (4) Emotional Continuity Factor
‚Äî
Normalized to 0‚Äì10
```

Input from:

* Ubuntuwa-NDAA

* Ubuntuwa-KANYE

* Ubuntuwa-MOYO
* Ubuntuwa-UMOYA
* Ubuntuwa-KANO

Collectively weighed and normalized.

* Founder removal

* Operational planning
* Implementation
* Local entity management

* Ethics / social legitimacy adjudication
* Community impact scoring
* Regulatory risk signals

* War-game execution
* Scoring
* Consequence triggering

**Capital Entities**

* Financial risk inputs
* Fund allocations within ruleset
* No governance veto

# üß≠ HOW TO READ THIS MAP

This taxonomy is structured by **functional layers**:

### üèõ Governance & Authority

The *rule-setting and enforcement layer* ‚Äî e.g., OVAC, BoC, CRC.

### üõ° War-Games & Resilience

The *survivability layer* ‚Äî execution, scoring, adversarial simulation.

### üåæ Ubuntuwa Commons Nodes

The *community legitimacy & social impact layer* ‚Äî including the new permanent war-games node U-LUNGARA.

### üè≠ Operational Coops

Business and production entities that must comply and participate in drills.

### üí∞ Capital & Investment

Funds and financial institutions that feed metrics but **do not govern**.

### üì£ Programs & Community Services

Domain-specific service/program nodes feeding risk and impact data.

### üß∞ Studios & Tools

Production and creative studios; execution environment but not governance.

### üóÉ System Components

Archive OS, indexing, immutable logging ‚Äî the *memory layer*.

### üíº Financial & Governance Systems

Financial control layer with explicit dashboards and checklists.

### üë• Members & Roles

Different *classes of people* with defined authority.

### üë• Teams & Squads

Execution units and teams.

### üîÅ Processes & Workflows

Defined operational flows and decision paths.

### üìä Analytics & Indicators

Quantitative metrics guiding decisions.

### ‚ö†Ô∏è Authority & Escalation

Internal flags and rules for escalation and overrides.

---

# USAGE

üßæ **Documents** ‚Äî use full name once, then acronym.
üß© **Archive OS** ‚Äî use acronyms as keys in metadata.
üìä **Dashboards** ‚Äî map acronyms to visual widgets.
ü§ñ **Code / Policy engines** ‚Äî treat acronyms as constants.

Below is a **complete, context-aligned description of how job design works in your federation ecosystem**, *including who stewards it, how roles are defined and classified, and how it connects to governance, archive, war-games, and operational continuity*.

This is **not generic HR theory** ‚Äî it is your own **institutional job design doctrine**.

---

# JOB DESIGN IN YOUR ECOSYSTEM

*(How work is defined, stewarded, governed, and evolved)*

---

## WHY JOB DESIGN MATTERS HERE

Your ecosystem does **not treat job design as HR paperwork**.
Job design is a **systemic artifact** that directly feeds:

* Governance clarity
* Authority boundaries
* Risk containment
* War-game readiness
* Archive traceability
* Crisis succession

In other words: *Job design isn‚Äôt just what people do ‚Äî it‚Äôs how the system quantifies capability and accountability.*

---

# WHO STEWARDS JOB DESIGN

Job design is a **joint process** stewarded by multiple roles/layers:

```
                        +--------------------+
                        |   OVAC (Governance)|
                        +---------+----------+
                                  |
           +----------------------+---------------------+
           |                                            |
  Ubuntuwa Commons Nodes                           HRMC (Human Resources &
      (Social & Legitimacy)                              Membership Council)
           |                                            |
    +------+------------+----------------------+         |
    |                   |                      |         |
  SM / Steward Teams   Boards                Archive    Squad Leads
   (Class B)                                 Office      & Members
```

### Key Stewards

1. **OVAC ‚Äî Operational & Value-Alignment Council**

   * Sets **job design doctrine**
   * Ratifies new role classes
   * Interprets authority boundaries

2. **HRMC ‚Äî Human Resources & Membership Council**

   * Operational steward of job design lifecycle
   * Ensures roles align with classes (A‚ÄìG)
   * Oversees classification, leveling, and deprecation

3. **Ubuntuwa Commons Nodes**

   * Provide **social & community legitimacy**
   * Validate job designs against community norms
   * Feed social legitimacy scores into war-game criteria

4. **Squad Leads / Stewards (Class B)**

   * Define functional outcomes
   * Identify competencies
   * Work with HRMC to finalize role designs

5. **Entity Boards**

   * Approve entity-level job designs
   * Ensure compliance with OVAC doctrine

6. **Archive Office**

   * Stores immutable job design artifacts
   * Ensures lineage and version history

---

# JOB DESIGN PROCESS (CONTROLLED WORKFLOW)

Job design follows a **defined lifecycle**:

```
Draft ‚Üí Review ‚Üí Approval ‚Üí Activation ‚Üí Archive ‚Üí Sunset / Revision
```

### 1) **Draft**

* Created by **Squad Lead + Steward**
* Defines:

  * Role purpose
  * Outcomes & deliverables
  * Authority scope
  * Required competencies
  * Decision boundaries
  * Accountability matrix

Draft must declare **entity, program, and level**.

---

### 2) **Review**

* Passed to:

  * HRMC (primary)
  * Ubuntuwa Commons rep (social legitimacy/readiness)
* Evaluated against:

  * Governance doctrine (OVAC)
  * War-games impact
  * Equity & fairness
  * Risk exposure

If flagged, sent back with comments.

---

### 3) **Approval**

* HRMC recommendations ‚Üí **Entity Board**
* Board submits to **OVAC** for doctrine alignment
* On approval, role becomes **Active**

---

### 4) **Activation**

* Role published to:

  * Archive OS (immutable record)
  * Entity HR systems
  * Squad assignments
  * Operational dashboards

---

### 5) **Archive**

* Stored as:

  * **Job Design Artifact (JDA)**
  * With version, approvals, and hashes
  * Linked to:

    * Entity
    * Squad
    * Role class
    * Authority boundaries

---

### 6) **Sunset / Revision**

* Roles are **not permanent**
* Triggered by:

  * War-game failures
  * Strategy shifts
  * Authority boundary violations
* Sunset routes:

  * Revise
  * Merge
  * Archive as historic
  * Retire

---

# ANATOMY OF A JOB DESIGN ARTIFACT

Each Job Design Artifact (JDA) contains:

```
JDA-<ENTITY>-<ROLE>-<VERSION>

1. Title
2. Class (A‚ÄìG)
3. Purpose Statement
4. Outcomes / KPIs
5. Authority Boundaries (decision tables referenced)
6. Competency Requirements
7. Reporting Lines
8. Escalation Paths
9. GOV/HRMC/Board Approvals
10. Archive Hash
```

Sample keys that must exist in every JDA:

```
role.purpose
role.outputs
role.responsibilities
role.authorityTableRefs[]
role.class
role.level
role.entity
role.status
role.versionHistory
```

---

# CLASSIFICATION RULES (ROLES ‚Üî MEMBER CLASSES)

| Class                    | Who Can Serve            | Authority Scope                       |
| ------------------------ | ------------------------ | ------------------------------------- |
| **Class A (Worker)**     | Task execution           | Follow                                |
| **Class B (Steward)**    | Squad-level coordination | Coordinate                            |
| **Class C (Governance)** | Oversight & signoff      | Approve                               |
| **Class D (Commons)**    | Social legitimacy        | Advise / Validate                     |
| **Class E (Founder)**    | Navigator                | Constrained (no unilateral authority) |
| **Class F (Capital)**    | Investors                | No governance authority               |
| **Class G (Future)**     | Apprentices / Fellows    | Learning + support                    |

Only certain roles are assignable to each class, and **authority boundaries are enforced via decision tables**.

---

# ROLE LEVELS & PROGRESSION (STANDARDIZED)

### Level Tiers

```
Tier 1 ‚Äî Entry/Contributor
Tier 2 ‚Äî Specialist
Tier 3 ‚Äî Lead
Tier 4 ‚Äî Steward / Coach
Tier 5 ‚Äî Principal / Architect
Tier 6 ‚Äî Strategic Steward
Tier 7 ‚Äî Governance / OVAC Liaison
```

Roles are placed in tiers based on:

* Complexity
* Decision authority
* Risk exposure
* Impact scale

Tiering is owned by HRMC + Board + Commons validity check.

### üóÉ Archive OS

* Versioned artifacts

### ‚öñ Decision Table Engine

* Authority boundaries are **linked references** to decision logic

### üìä Operational Dashboards

### üìà Performance & Risk Engine

* Role design inputs expected performance risk
* War-games test structural robustness

### üìÖ Scheduler

  * Quarterly operation drills
  * War-games

# WAR-GAMES IMPACT ON JOB DESIGN

LUNGARA exams stress **role boundaries**:

* Do responsibilities hold under shock?
* Are authority limits respected?
* Does social legitimacy score change if roles fail?
* What happens if role is absent in crisis simulations?

Failures in these metrics trigger **role revisions or design sunsets**.

---

# AUTHORITY BOUNDARY IN JOB DESIGN

Each role includes **authority references**:

```
role.authorityTableRefs = [ A01, A05, C14‚Ä¶ ]
```

These map to decision table IDs such as:

* decisions about capital spending
* crisis escalation
* role intervention limits
* compensation rights

A job is ‚Äúactive‚Äù only if its authority references are valid for the member class.

---

# REVISION & SUNSET TRIGGERS

üîπ War-game failure implicates role boundaries
üîπ Economic shift requires structural changes
üîπ Regulatory attack alters risk models
üîπ Authority breach logged in Archive
üîπ Social legitimacy drops below threshold

When triggered:

* Role enters **Sunset Pending**
* Governance review is scheduled
* Option: Revise or Retire

# JOB & ROLE LIFECYCLE FRAMEWORK

*(Design ‚Üí Activation ‚Üí Management ‚Üí Sunset)*

This framework governs all job constructs in your federation.

## KEY OVERSIGHT BODIES

| Accountable Steward                              | Domain                                   |
| ------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------- |
| **HRMC** ‚Äî Human Resources & Membership Council  | Operational job lifecycle governance     |

# 1) ROLE DEFINITIONS

In your ecosystem:

* **Job** = a *named work construct* with explicit outcomes
* **Role** = *functional responsibilities and authorities*
* **Position** = *explicit slot filled by a person*
* **Steward** = *role owner and coordinator*
* **Squad** = *team aligned to outcomes*

These maps align to classes (A‚ÄìG) per Member Role Doctrine.

---

# 2) JOB/ROLE LIFECYCLE STATES

```
DRAFT ‚Üí REVIEW ‚Üí APPROVED ‚Üí ACTIVE ‚Üí REVIEW/CYCLE ‚Üí RETIRED
```

Each state is tracked in **Archive OS** as an immutable object with references:

```
RoleArtifact
 ‚îú‚îÄ role_id
 ‚îú‚îÄ status
 ‚îú‚îÄ version
 ‚îú‚îÄ authority_refs
 ‚îú‚îÄ archive_hash
```

---

# 3) WHO STEWARDS THE STANDARDS

### **A) Framework Steward ‚Äî HRMC**

HRMC is the **primary steward of job standards**. Responsibilities:

* Maintain job taxonomy
* Define required competencies
* Map roles to decision tables
* Ensure authority boundaries
* Publish templates

HRMC issues:

* **Job Design Templates**
* **Role Authority Linkage Specs**
* **Skill & Competency Matrix**
* **Position Lifecycle Policies**

---

### **B) Doctrine Authority ‚Äî OVAC**

Risk context or structural conflict? OVAC steps in to:

* Approve framework changes
* Mediate disputes over authority boundaries
* Adjust lifecycle triggers
* Rule on inter-entity job design issues

OVAC action is required for:

* Any job design that affects governance authority
* Executive role definitions
* Cross-entity authority bridges

---

### **C) Social Norms Steward ‚Äî Ubuntuwa Commons Council**

For job constructs that affect community or narrative domains:

* Validate ethical fit
* Assess impact on legitimacy
* Provide social legitimacy scores

Commons input factors into **LUNGARA war-games** as social legitimacy metrics.

---

### **D) Local Execution ‚Äî Entity Board**

Entity boards:

* Apply job designs locally
* Confirm fit with entity mission
* Review and approve ‚ÄúActive‚Äù status
* Provide entity-specific custom fields

Local board approval is required *after* HRMC/template alignment.

---

### **E) Record Integrity ‚Äî Archive Office**

Every change is archived immutably with:

* Version history
* Approval chain
* Authority references
* Link to decision tables

This allows historical traceability and audit readiness.

---

# 4) PROCESS ‚Äî STEP BY STEP

---

## A. **Job Drafting**

(Lead: Squad Lead / Steward)

### Inputs:

* Role purpose
* Outputs/KPIs
* Authority scope (decision table refs)
* Competencies
* Reporting & escalation paths

### Deliverable:

* **Draft Role Artifact**

Stored in Archive OS as **DRAFT** with hash & timestamp.

---

## B. **Review by HRMC**

HRMC validates:

| Dimension            | Check                  |
| -------------------- | ---------------------- |
| Authority boundaries | vs. decision tables    |
| Role class           | (A‚ÄìG mapping)          |
| Competency match     | against skill taxonomy |
| Risk exposure        | via archive inputs     |
| Social impact        | preliminary check      |

HRMC either:

* Returns Draft with comments
* Advances Review status

---

## C. **Ubuntuwa Commons Validation** *(optional but required if social impact is medium/high)*

Role artifacts flagged by HRMC for social/vulnerability domain are reviewed by **Ubuntuwa Commons Council**:

| Social Risk Level | Commons Required? |
| ----------------- | ----------------- |
| High              | Yes               |
| Medium            | Yes               |
| Low               | Optional          |

Their input is archived as a *Social Legitimacy Stamp* with score.

---

## D. **OVAC Doctrine Advisory** *(if needed)*

If HRMC or Commons identify conflict with governance doctrine, OVAC adjudicates. Possible mandates:

* Adjust authority boundaries
* Alter escalation paths
* Restrict role authority

---

## E. **Entity Board Approval**

Once HRMC (and Commons/OVAC if applicable) greenlights, entity board:

* Approves the artifact for ‚ÄúActive‚Äù
* Assigns local categories
* Maps budget line items

---

## F. **Activation**

Updated status:

```
Status: ACTIVE
Published to:
  - Squad plans
  - Entity org model
  - Archive OS (immutable)
```

Archive entries now include all approval chain hashes.

---

## G. **Maintenance & Review**

Periodic review nodes:

| Trigger                   | Interval           |
| ------------------------- | ------------------ |
| Operational review        | Quarterly          |
| War-games impact review   | Per war-game cycle |
| Governance / risk update  | Monthly            |
| Authority boundary change | As required        |

---

## H. **Retirement / Sunset**

Roles/jobs are retired if:

* Redundant
* Failed war-game tests
* Structural change
* Legal/regulatory change
* Social legitimacy collapse

Process:

```
Active ‚Üí Sunset Pending ‚Üí Retired
```

Retirement artifacts include:

* Sunset rationale
* Archive hash
* Legacy linkages

---

# 5) ROLES & AUTHORITY BOUNDARIES

Each job definition must explicitly declare **authority references**:

```
"authorityRefs": ["A02", "C05", "O13"]
```

These map to your **decision tables**, ensuring that jobs only have pre-authorized decision scopes.

Authority binding examples:

| Role              | Allowed Authority        | Forbidden                    |
| ----------------- | ------------------------ | ---------------------------- |
| Squad Lead        | Approve tasks            | Capital acceptance           |
| Steward Member    | Coordinate strategy      | Override OVAC                |
| Governance Member | Approve doctrine         | Execute operations           |
| Commons Member    | Social legitimacy review | Command squads               |
| Founder Member    | Mission guidance         | Emergency authority override |

Decision tables enforce this programmatically during war-games and real operations.

---

# 6) JOB ARCHIVE & VERSIONING

Every job artifact lives in Archive OS with:

```
{
  "roleId": "<uuid>",
  "status": "DRAFT/ACTIVE/RETIRED",
  "versions": [
      {
         "version": "v1.0",
         "hash": "<hash>",
         "approvals": ["HRMC", "Board"],
         "timestamp": "..."
      }
  ],
  "decisionTableRefs": [...],
  "competencies": [...],
  "archiveHash": "..."
}
```

Immutable history = audit & compliance readiness.

---

# 7) WAR-GAMES (LUNGARA) INTEGRATION

LUNGARA war-games stress test job/role definitions to assess:

* Role absence shock
* Authority boundary violations
* Social legitimacy collapse
* Red Team influence

Roles that *fail* war-game conditions are:

* Marked **Review Pending**
* Flagged for revision
* Possible sunset

LUNGARA triggers become **revision events**.

# HUMAN RESOURCES IN YOUR FEDERATION

*(How HR works across both Ubuntuwa Commons and Cooperative Entities)*

HR in your system is a **governed, disciplined, and system-embedded function** that interlocks with:

‚úî Governance (OVAC)
‚úî Commons legitimacy
‚úî Job design & authority tables
‚úî Archive OS
‚úî War-games (LUNGARA)
‚úî Member classes & lifecycle
‚úî Capital & compliance

No HR action is autonomous without **policy, authority linkage, and archive traceability**.

---

# HR‚ÄôS PURPOSE IN THE FEDERATION

Human Resources is **not just hiring, firing, and payroll**.

It is defined by these core functions:

1. **Job & Role Lifecycle Management**
   ‚Äî Design, approve, revise, retire jobs.

2. **Membership Lifecycle Management**
   ‚Äî Onboarding, transitions between classes, exits.

3. **Authority & Role Assignment Enforcement**
   ‚Äî Ensuring people have *only* the authority their roles grant.

4. **Performance & Risk Evaluation**
   ‚Äî Linking war-games outcomes to capability design.

5. **Competency Mapping & Development**
   ‚Äî Building skill taxonomies tied to roles.

6. **Compliance & Regulatory HR Operations**
   ‚Äî Tax, labor classifications, co-op law.

7. **Conflict & Incident Processing**
   ‚Äî Whistleblower handling, grievances, behavioral risks.

8. **Cultural & Commons Alignment**
   ‚Äî Ubuntuwa norms and ethics embedded in every HR action.

9. **Succession & Continuity Management**
   ‚Äî Especially for key roles and crises.

10. **Archive Integration & Immutable Logging**
    ‚Äî Every HR artifact becomes an Archive OS object.

# HR GOVERNANCE STACK

HR in the federation is stewarded by **multiple layers**, each with clear mandate and authority limits:

```
       +------------------+ 
       |      OVAC        |   ‚Üí Doctrine authority / final arbitrator
       +------------------+
                  |
   +-----------------------------+
   |     HRMC ‚Äî Human Resources  |   ‚Üí Core HR process owner
   |     & Membership Council    |
   +-----------------------------+
      /         |             \
 Ubuntuwa     Entity         Archive
Commons       Boards         Office
Council       & Stewards     (logging)
```
